قال وان وطى المكاتب امة على وجه الملك بغير اذن المولى ثم استحقها رجل فعليه العقر يوخذ به في الكتابة وان وطيها على وجه النكاح لم يؤخذ به حتى يعتق و كذلك الماذون له ووجه الفرق ان في الفصل الاول ظهر الدين فى حق المولى لان التجارة وتوابعها داخلة تحت الكتابة وهذا العقر من توابعها لأنه لولا الشراء لما سقط الحد وما لم يسقط الحد لا يجب العقر اما لم يظهر فى الفصل الثاني لان النكاح ليس من الاكتساب في شيء فلا ينتظمه الكتابة كالكفالة. قال واذا اشترى المكاتب جارية شراء فاسدا ثم وطيها فردها أخذ بالعقر في المكاتبة وكذلك العبد المأذون له لانه من باب التجارة فان التصرف تارة يقع صحيحا ومرة يقع فاسدا والكتابة والاذن ينتظمانه بنوعيه كالتوكيل فكان ظاهرا في حق المولى
ترجمہ اگر ولی کی مکاتب نے کسی باندی سے ملک کے طور پر آقا کی اجازت کے بغیر پھر کوئی شخص اس کا مستحق نکل آیا تو مکاتب پر عقر واجب ہوگا جس کا مواخذہ حالت کتابت میں ہوگا اور اگر نکاح کے طور پر وطی کی تو عقر کا مواخذہ نہ ہوگا یہاں تک کہ وہ آزاد ہو جائے اور اس طرح عبد ماذون ہے۔ وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ پہلی صورت میں دین آقا کے حق میں ظاہر ہو گیا ۔ کیونکہ تجارت اور اس کے توابع کتابت کے تحت میں داخل ہیں اور یہ عقر توابع تجارت میں سے ہے۔ اس لئے کہ اگر خرید نہ ہوتی تو حد زناء ساقط نہ ہوتی اور جب تک حد ساقط نہ ہو عقر واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ لیکن دوسری صورت میں دین ظاہر نہیں ہوا کیونکہ نکاح اکتساب میں سے نہیں ہے تو کفالت کی طرح کتابت اس کو شامل نہ ہوگی ۔ اگر مکاتب نے شراء فاسد کے طور سے باندی خرید کر اس سے وطی کی پھر اس کو واپس کر دیا تو عقر کا مواخذہ حالت مکاتبت میں ہوگا۔ ایسے ہی عبد ماذون ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ باب تجارت سے ہے اس لئے کہ تصرف کبھی صحیح اور کبھی فاسد واقع ہوتا ہے اور اذن وکتابت دونوں قسموں کو شامل ہے۔ جیسے وکیل کرنے میں ہے پس یہ آقا کے حق میں بھی ظاہر ہوگا۔ تشریح قوله وان وطى المكاتب الخ - مکاتب یا عبد ماذون نے ایک باندی خریدی اور یہ خیال کرتے ہوئے کہ جب میں نے خریدی ہے تو میری ہی ہے اس سے صحبت کر لی پھر باندی کسی اور کی نکلی تو مکاتب یا عبد ماذون پر عقر یعنی اس وطی کا عوض مہر فی الحال واجب ہوگا آزادی تک مؤخر نہ ہوگا ۔ اور اگر باندی کے ساتھ نکاح کر کے وطی کی ہو تو عقر آزادی کے بعد دینا ہوگا۔ وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ شراء کی صورت میں دین مہر آقا کے حق میں ظاہر ہو چکا اس واسطے کہ تجارت اور توابع تجارت یعنی ضیافت وغیرہ سب تحت العقد داخل ہیں اور عقر بھی توابع تجارت میں سے ہے۔ اس لئے کہ اگر شراء وخرید نہ ہوتی تو اس کے ذمہ سے حد زنا ساقط نہ ہوتی اور جب تک حد زنا ساقط نہ ہو تب تک عقر واجب نہیں ہوتا ۔ بخلاف نکاح کے کہ نکاح کی صورت میں دین مہر آقا کے حق میں ظاہر نہیں ہوا۔ کیونکہ نکاح از قبیل اکتساب نہیں ہے تو عقد کتابت نکاح کو شامل نہ ہوا جیسے کفالت کرنے کو شامل نہیں ہوتا چنانچہ اگر مکاتب نے کسی شخص کی مالی کفالت کر لی تو اس سے مال کا دعویٰ فی الحال نہیں ہو سکتا۔ جب تک کہ آزاد نہ ہو جائے کیوں کہ یہ عقد کتابت میں داخل نہیں ہے۔ لہذا عقر آزادی کے بعد دینا ہوگا۔
قوله بغير اذن المولى الخ - يقید اس لئے لگائی ہے تا کہ اس سے اذن آقا کی صورت میں اس حکم کا فائدہ واضح ہو جائے کہ اذن کی صورت میں مواخذہ بطریق اولی ہو گا۔ نیز اگر وہ ماذون بالنکاح ہو اور نکاح کر کے وطی کرے تو اس سے مہر کا مواخذہ فی الحال ہوگا اور اگر ماذون بالنکاح نہ ہو تو مواخذہ فی الحال نہیں ہوگا بلکہ آزادی کے بعد تک مؤخر ہوگا۔
قوله واذا اشترى المكاتب الخ - اگر مکاتب یا عبد ماذون نے باندی بطریق شراء فاسد خرید کر اس سے وطی کر لی ۔ پھر وہ فساد عقد کی وجہ سے مالک کو واپس کر دی گئی تو عقر فی الحال واجب ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ فاسد خریداری بھی از قسم تجارت ہے۔ کیونکہ تصرف کبھی صحیح واقع ہوتا ہے اور کبھی فاسد ۔ اور کتابت واذن تجارت تصرف کی ان دونوں قسموں کو شامل ہے جیسے توکیل میں ہوتا ہے کہ وکیل مطلق کو تصرف صحیح و تصرف فاسد ہر دو کا اختیار ہوتا ہے۔ پس گویا آقا نے اس کی اجازت دے دی۔ لہذا یہ تاوان آقا کے حق میں بھی ظاہر ہوگا۔
He said: If the mukatab has intercourse with a slave woman on the basis of ownership without the master's permission, then a man claims her, then upon him is the 'aqr (compensation), taken in the kitaba. If he has intercourse with her on the basis of marriage, it is not taken until he becomes free. Similarly for the authorized slave. The difference is that in the first case, the debt appears in the master's right because trade and its appendages are included in the kitaba, and this 'aqr is from its appendages, because if not for the purchase, the hadd would not be dropped, and as long as the hadd is not dropped, the 'aqr is not obligatory. In the second case, it does not appear because marriage is not from earnings, so the kitaba does not encompass it, like suretyship. He said: If the mukatab buys a slave woman with a fasid (invalid) purchase, then has intercourse with her and returns her, the 'aqr is taken in the kitaba. Similarly for the authorized slave, because it is from the category of trade; transactions sometimes occur validly and sometimes invalidly, and the kitaba and authorization encompass both types, like in agency, so it appears in the master's right. Translation: If a mukatab, without the master's permission, has intercourse with a slave woman on the basis of ownership, then a person emerges as her rightful owner, then the 'aqr is obligatory on the mukatab and is taken in the kitaba. If he has intercourse on the basis of marriage, the 'aqr is not taken until he becomes free. Similarly for an authorized slave. The difference is that in the first case, the debt appears in the master's right because trade and its appendages are included in the kitaba, and this 'aqr is from the appendages of trade. Reason: If the purchase had not occurred, the hadd of zina would not be dropped, and until the hadd is dropped, the 'aqr is not obligatory. But in the second case, the debt does not appear because marriage is not from earnings, so the kitaba does not include it, like suretyship. If the mukatab buys a slave woman through a fasid purchase and then has intercourse, then returns her, the 'aqr is taken in the kitaba. Similarly for an authorized slave. This is because it is from the category of trade; transactions sometimes are valid and sometimes invalid, and authorization and kitaba encompass both types, as in agency. Thus, it appears in the master's right. Commentary on 'He said: If the mukatab...' — A mukatab or authorized slave buys a slave woman, thinking she is his, and has intercourse. Then the slave woman turns out to belong to someone else. Then the 'aqr, i.e., the mahr-like compensation for the intercourse, is obligatory immediately on the mukatab or authorized slave, not deferred until freedom. If he married the slave woman and had intercourse, then the 'aqr is due after freedom. The difference: In the case of purchase, the debt of mahr appears in the master's right because trade and its appendages, such as hospitality, are all included in the contract, and the 'aqr is also from the appendages of trade. If the purchase had not occurred, the hadd of zina would not be dropped from his liability, and until the hadd of zina is dropped, the 'aqr is not obligatory. Unlike marriage, where the debt of mahr does not appear in the master's right because marriage is not from the category of earnings, so the kitaba contract does not include marriage, just as it does not include suretyship. For example, if the mukatab gave a financial surety for someone, he cannot be immediately sued for the money until he becomes free, because that is not included in the kitaba. Therefore, the 'aqr is given after freedom. Statement: 'Without the master's permission' etc. — This condition is placed so that from it the benefit of the ruling in the case of permission becomes clear: that with permission, accountability occurs a fortiori. Also, if he is authorized for marriage and marries and has intercourse, then the mahr is taken immediately; if he is not authorized for marriage, it is not taken immediately but deferred until after freedom. Statement: 'If the mukatab buys...' — If a mukatab or authorized slave buys a slave woman through a fasid purchase and has intercourse, then she is returned to the owner due to the invalidity of the contract, then the 'aqr is obligatory immediately. This is because a fasid purchase is also from the category of trade. Transactions sometimes occur validly and sometimes invalidly, and the kitaba and authorization for trade encompass both types, as in agency where an absolute agent has the right to both valid and invalid transactions. So it is as if the master permitted him. Hence this compensation appears in the master's right.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary of Al-Hidayah. It discusses the liability for 'aqr (a compensation due for intercourse with a slave woman) when a mukatab (a slave with a kitaba contract) or a ma'dhun (authorized slave) has intercourse with a slave woman without the master's permission. Two scenarios are distinguished: (1) if the intercourse was done on the belief of ownership (e.g., having purchased her), then the 'aqr is due immediately and can be taken in the kitaba; (2) if it was done through marriage, the 'aqr is not taken until after the mukatab becomes free. The reasoning ('illa) is that in the first case, the transaction (purchase) falls under trade, which is within the scope of the kitaba. The 'aqr is considered an appendage of trade because without the purchase, the mukatab would be liable for the hadd (fixed punishment) of zina, and the 'aqr is incurred to avoid that hadd. Since the kitaba encompasses trade and its appendages, the debt (including the 'aqr) appears in the master's right and is payable from the kitaba. In contrast, marriage is not a trade activity, so it is not included in the kitaba. Hence, the 'aqr is not collectible until the mukatab is free, similar to suretyship (kafala), which is also not included. The passage then extends this to a fasid (invalid) purchase: since a fasid transaction is still a form of trade, the same rule applies. The kitaba and authorization encompass both valid and invalid transactions, analogous to an absolute agent (wakil mutlaq) who can engage in both valid and invalid contracts. The addition of 'without the master's permission' in the matn is to highlight that permission would make the liability a fortiori (bi tariq al-awla). If the slave is authorized for marriage (ma'dhun bi al-nikah) then the 'aqr for marriage is also taken immediately.

Key Terms
العقر (al-'aqr): Compensation for intercourse with a slave woman, similar to mahr for free women, paid to the owner for the reduction in value or for the sexual act.
المكاتب (al-mukatab): A slave who has entered into a kitaba contract with the master, agreeing to pay a sum for freedom.
المأذون (al-ma'dhun): A slave authorized by the master to engage in trade; his transactions are valid within the scope of authorization.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a mukatab has intercourse with a slave woman on the basis of purchase without the master's permission, and then the woman is claimed by another, when is the 'aqr taken?
A) Immediately in the kitaba
B) Only after he becomes free
C) Only after the master claims it
D) It is not taken

Key Takeaway
The 'aqr for a mukatab's intercourse is taken immediately in the kitaba if based on trade (purchase or fasid purchase), but deferred until freedom if based on marriage, because marriage is not part of trade.

Mukatabah's Option Upon Childbirth and Her 'Aqr
Ruling on mukatabah's khiyar and taking 'aqr from master

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mukatabah's khiyar when she gives birth, explain the 'illah for the option, and describe the Hanafi ruling on her taking 'aqr from the master.

Core Idea
A mukatabah who bears a child from her master chooses between immediate freedom with payment or deferred freedom without; if she continues kitabah, she takes 'aqr.

This lesson examines the legal position of a female mukatab (a slave under a contract of manumission) who gives birth to her master's child. The Hanafi school gives her a unique option (khiyar) between two paths to freedom, and if she chooses to continue the kitabah, she is entitled to a compensation called 'aqr. Understanding this ruling reveals how the school balances the rights of the master and the mukatabah through istihsan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Event and Subject
Focus on the scenario: a female mukatab gives birth to a child conceived with her master. This triggers special legal consequences.
The mukatabah is a slave who has a contract (kitabah) to earn her freedom by paying installments.
2
State the Ruling on the Option
The text states she has a choice (khiyar): she may continue with the kitabah (immediate freedom upon payment) or declare incapacity (ta'jiz) and become an umm walad (deferred freedom upon master's death).
This is a mubah (permissible) option; she is not forced to choose either.
3
Analyze the 'Illah (Legal Cause)
The reason for the option is that she has encountered two 'directions' to freedom: one immediate with a payment (kitabah), and one deferred without payment (umm walad). The choice allows her to select the path that suits her best.
The 'illah is explicitly mentioned in the text: 'because she has encountered two directions of freedom'.
4
Understand the Child's Status and Master's Role
Regardless of her choice, the child's lineage is established with the master and is free. This is because the master has the authority to claim paternity (istilad), and his partial ownership over the mukatabah is sufficient for this purpose.
Istilad requires a claim (da'wa) by the master; here it is implied upon birth.
5
Identify the Ruling on 'Aqr if She Continues Kitabah
If she chooses to continue the kitabah, she takes the 'aqr (a dower-like compensation) from the master. The basis is her exclusive right over herself and her benefits, as established in earlier discussions of kitabah.
The 'aqr is wajib upon the master. It is distinct from mahr, as it compensates for intercourse with a partially-owned slave.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا ولدت المكاتبة من المولى فهى بالخيار ان شاءت مضت على الكتابة وان شاءت عجزت نفسها وصارت ام ولد له لانها تلقتها جهتا حرية عاجلة ببدل وآجلة بغير بدل فتخير بينهما ونسب ولدها ثابت من المولى وهو حر لان المولى يملك الاعتاق فى ولدها وماله من الملك يكفى لصحة الاستيلاد بالدعوة واذا مضت على الكتابة اخذت العقر من مولاها لاختصاصها بنفسها وبمنافعها على ما قدمنا
And when the female mukatab gives birth from the master, she has the choice: if she wishes, she continues upon the kitabah, and if she wishes, she declares herself incapable and becomes an umm walad for him, because she has encountered two directions of freedom: one immediate with a payment, and one deferred without a payment, so she chooses between them. And the lineage of her child is established from the master, and he is free, because the master possesses the power to free her child, and his ownership is sufficient for the validity of istilad by claim. And if she continues upon the kitabah, she takes the 'aqr from her master, due to her exclusive right over herself and her benefits, as we have previously presented.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Mukatab presents a ruling on a female mukatab who gives birth to a child from her master. It states that she has an option (khiyar): she may either continue with her kitabah contract, paying the installments and gaining immediate freedom, or she may declare herself incapable (ta'jiz) of fulfilling the kitabah and become an umm walad (mother of a child of the master), which grants her deferred freedom upon the master's death. The reason ('illa) is that she has acquired two avenues to freedom: one immediate but with payment (the kitabah route), and one deferred without payment (the umm walad route). The commentary explains that the child's lineage is established with the master regardless of whether the birth occurs at six months or later, and the child is free by consensus. This is because the master can free the child by claiming paternity, and his ownership over the mukatabah, though incomplete (since she has rights over herself), is sufficient for valid istilad (claiming the child as his own). If she chooses to continue with kitabah, she is entitled to take the 'aqr (dower-like compensation) from the master, because she exclusively owns herself and her benefits, as established earlier. The commentary notes that Imam Malik, Ahmad ibn Hanbal, and in one narration Imam al-Shafi'i agree with the Hanafi position on the 'aqr, though others may differ.

Key Terms
عقر ('aqr): The compensation (dower-like payment) owed by the master to the mukatabah for intercourse, taken when she continues with kitabah.
ام ولد (umm walad): A female slave who bears a child to her master; she becomes free upon the master's death.
استيلاد (istilad): The master's act of claiming paternity of a child born to his female slave, which makes the child free and the mother an umm walad.
خيار (khiyar): The option or choice given to the mukatabah to select between two legal paths to freedom.
تعجيز (ta'jiz): The mukatabah's declaration of inability to fulfill the kitabah contract, which renders her an umm walad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the reason ('illah) for the mukatabah's option to either continue with kitabah or become umm walad?
A) She has two directions of freedom: one immediate with payment and one deferred without payment.
B) The master can free the child in both cases.
C) She owns herself completely.
D) The kitabah contract is invalidated by childbirth.

Key Takeaway
A mukatabah who bears her master's child may choose between immediate freedom with payment (continuing kitabah) or deferred freedom without (becoming umm walad); if she chooses the former, she takes the 'aqr as compensation.

Rulings on Mukatabah's Death and Second Child
Rulings on death of parties and additional child in mukatabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings when a mukatabah dies with or without wealth, and apply qiyas to determine whether a second unclaimed child must perform sa'yah.

Core Idea
A second child of a mukatabah, if unclaimed by the master, follows the mother's kitabah status and must perform sa'yah.

This passage from al-Hidayah continues the discussion of mukatabah (a female slave with a kitabah contract). It addresses three distinct scenarios: the master's death, the mukatabah's death with wealth, and her death without wealth when she has a second child. The author uses analogy (qiyas) to extend the rule of a male mukatab's child to the second child of a mukatabah. Understanding these rulings requires careful attention to the status of each child and the master's paternity claim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage covers: (1) master dies → she becomes free by istilad, kitabah drops; (2) she dies with wealth → kitabah paid from estate, remainder to son; (3) she dies without wealth and has a second unclaimed child → child performs sa'yah.
2
Understand the first scenario: master's death
If the master dies, the mukatabah becomes an umm walad and is freed automatically; the kitabah debt is discharged because it is no longer owed.
This is by consensus.
3
Analyze the second scenario: mukatabah dies with wealth
Her estate pays the kitabah first (as a debt), and any remainder goes to her free son as inheritance. No sa'yah on the son because he is already free.
4
Examine the third scenario: no wealth and second child
If she has a second child from the master, the child is not automatically claimed by the master. Unless the master claims paternity, the child is not his free child. Upon her death without fulfilling kitabah, this child must perform sa'yah to pay off the debt.
The child becomes a subsidiary mukatab (mukatab taba'an).
5
Apply the qiyas and note the exception
The ruling is based on qiyas with a male mukatab's child: just as a child of a deceased male mukatab follows him in kitabah, so does the second child of a mukatabah. However, if the master dies after the child's sa'yah starts, the child becomes free and sa'yah drops, because he is treated like an umm walad's child.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم ان مات المولى عتقت بالاستيلاد وسقط عنها بدل الكتابة وان ماتت هى وتركت مالا تودى منه مكاتبتها وما بقى ميراث لابنها جريا على موجب الكتابة فان لم تترك مالا فلا سعاية على الولد لانه حر ولو ولدت ولدا آخر لم يلزم المولى الا ان يدعى لحرمة وطيها عليه فلو لم يدع وماتت من غير وفاء يسعى هذا الولد لانه مکاتب تبعًا لها فلومات المولى بعد ذلك عتق وبطل عنه السعاية لانه بمنزلة ام الولد اذهو ولدها فيتبعها
Then if the master dies, she becomes free by istilad and the kitabah payment drops from her. And if she dies and leaves wealth, her kitabah is paid from it, and what remains is inheritance for her son, proceeding according to the requirement of kitabah. If she does not leave wealth, there is no sa'yah upon the son because he is free. And if she gives birth to another child, it does not become binding upon the master unless he claims [it], because intercourse with her is forbidden for him. So if he does not claim and she dies without payment, this child performs sa'yah because he is a mukatab in her following. Then if the master dies after that, he becomes free and the sa'yah drops from him, because he is in the position of an umm walad's child, since he is her child and follows her.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion from the previous section. It addresses three scenarios: (1) If the master dies after the mukatabah has chosen to continue with kitabah, she becomes free automatically as an umm walad (since her child established her status), and the kitabah payment is discharged. This is by consensus. (2) If the mukatabah dies before completing kitabah and leaves wealth, her estate is used to fulfill the kitabah payment (as a debt), and any remainder goes to her child as inheritance, since the child is free and inherits as normal. If she leaves no wealth, there is no obligation (sa'yah) on the child to work to pay off the kitabah because he is free and not a slave. (3) If she gives birth to a second child (from the master), this child does not automatically become a free child of the master unless the master claims paternity. This is because intercourse with a mukatabah is haram for the master (since she is not his exclusive property entirely). If the master does not claim, and the mukatabah dies without fulfilling the kitabah, this second child must perform sa'yah (work to earn money) to pay off the kitabah debt, because he follows the status of his mother and becomes a subsidiary mukatab (mukatab taba'). If the master later dies, this second child becomes free (like an umm walad's child) and the sa'yah obligation drops, because he is treated as a child of an umm walad who follows his mother's status.

Key Terms
سعاية (sa'yah): The effort or earning required from a mukatab (or following child) to pay off the kitabah debt.
مکاتب تبعا (mukatab taba'an): A person who becomes a mukatab by following the status of a parent who is a mukatab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if a mukatabah dies without wealth and has a second child not claimed by the master?
A) The child is free and has no obligation.
B) The child must perform sa'yah to pay off the kitabah.
C) The master must pay the remaining kitabah.
D) The first child becomes responsible for the kitabah.

Key Takeaway
A second unclaimed child of a mukatabah follows her kitabah status and must perform sa'yah unless the master later dies, freeing the child.

Mukatabah Gives Birth: Child's Freedom and Mother's Choice
Rulings on mukatabah giving birth and child's status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings regarding a mukatabah's child's lineage and freedom, and explain the mukatabah's choice to remain under kitaba or become umm walad.

Core Idea
A mukatabah's child is free and lineage from the master; the mother has two paths to freedom.

This lesson examines the Hanafi rulings when a female slave under kitaba (mukatabah) gives birth. The child's status and the mother's newly acquired dual entitlement to freedom are clarified. We will see why the child is free regardless of the mother's kitaba, and how she gains the option to either complete her kitaba or become an umm walad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The passage rules that when a mukatabah gives birth, the child is free and its lineage is established from the master. The mother has a choice: remain on kitaba or become umm walad.
This is a combined ruling on status and option.
2
Understand the mother's dual right to freedom
The commentary explains she has two avenues: kitaba (contract) and istilad (becoming umm walad). Hence she can choose.
This is a key Hanafi principle: overlapping causes of freedom.
3
Trace the dalil for the child's freedom
The master could free the child directly, so claiming lineage (which implies freeing) is a fortiori. Qiyas: if master can free another's child, he can certainly free his own.
Proof is analogical reasoning (qiyas awlawi).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب المكاتب
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲ ہوگا۔ مقتضائے کتابت پر چلتے ہوئے اور اگر اس نے کچھ مال نہیں چھوڑا تو بچہ پر سعایت نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ وہ آزاد ہے۔ اور اگر اسنے دوسرا بچہ جنا تو ہر آقا کے ذمہ لازم نہ ہوگا ۔ مگر یہ کہ وہ دعوی کرے کیونکہ آقا پر مکاتبہ کی وطی حرام ہے۔ اب اگر آقا نے بچہ کا دعویٰ نہیں کیا اور مکاتبہ کچھ چھوڑے بغیر مرگئی تو یہ دوسرا بچہ سعایت کرے گا۔ اس لئے کہ وہ ماں کے تابع ہو کر مکاتب ہے۔ پھر اگر اس کے بعد آ قا مر جائے تو یہ بچہ آزاد ہو جائے گا اور اس کے ذمہ سے سعایت ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ یہ بچہ بمنزلہ ولد کے ہے اس لئے کہ وہ ام ولد کا بچہ ہے تو اسی کے تابع ہوگا۔
تشریح قوله واذا ولدت ... الخ - آقا نے اپنی باندی کو مکاتب کیا اور اس سے بچہ ہوا تو باندی کو اختیار ہے چاہے عقد کتابت پر باقی رہے اور بدل کتابت ادا کر کے فی الحال آزاد ہو جائے اور چاہے خود کو عاجز کر کے ام ولد ر ہے۔ اور آقا کے انتقال کے بعد آزاد ہو جائے ۔ وجہ اختیار یہ ہے کہ اس کو دو جہتوں سے حق حریت حاصل ہو گیا۔ ایک کتابت کی جہت سے اور ایک ام ولد ہو جانے کی جہت سے پس اس کو دونوں کا اختیار ہوگا۔
قوله ونسب ولدها .... الخ - مکاتبہ مذکورہ کے بچہ کا نسب آقا سے ثابت ہوگا۔ خواہ اس کی پیدائش چھ ماہ پر ہوئی ہو یا اس سے زائد پر۔ اور وہ بچہ آزاد ہوگا جس میں کوئی اختلاف نہیں ہے وجہ یہ ہے کہ آقا اس کے بچہ کو آزاد کر سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ آقا کی جانب سے نسب کا دعوی مثل تحریر کے ہے اور جب آقا بالقصد اس کے اس بچہ کو آزاد کر سکتا ہے جو خود اس کے نطفہ سے نہیں ہے تو دعوی نسب کے ضمن میں بطریق اولی کر سکتا ہے۔
قوله وماله من الملک الخ - لفظ مالہ مسیح کلام ہے ای والذی لہ اور من الملک ما کا بیان ہے۔ اس قول سے صاحب ہدایہ کا مقصد ایک وہم کا ازالہ ہے۔ وہم یہ ہوتا ہے کہ مکاتبہ میں جو آقا کی ملک ہے وہ ناقص ہے۔ لہذا اس کی طرف سے دعوی نسب صحیح ہونا چاہیے۔ موصوف فرماتے ہیں کہ آقا کو مکاتبہ باندی میں جو ملک رقبہ حاصل ہے وہ صحت دعوئی استیلا د کے لئے کافی ہے گو اس کو ملک ید حاصل نہ ہو۔ وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ آقا کی یہ ملک بہر حال اس ملک سے قوی تر ہے۔ جو مکاتب کو اپنی مکاتبہ میں حاصل ہوتی ہے۔ بدلیل آنکہ آقا کا اپنی مکاتبہ کو آزاد کر نا صیح ہے اور مکاتب کا آزاد کر ناصحیح نہیں۔ اور مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مکاتب اگر اپنی مکاتبہ کے بچہ کا نسب کا دعوی کرے تو اس سے نسب ثابت ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس جب آقا مدعی نسب ہو تو بطریق اولی ثابت ہوگا۔
قوله واذا مضت ... الخ - آغاز مسئلہ میں یہ بات معلوم ہوگئی تھی کہ مکاتبہ مذکورہ کود و اختیار ہیں ۔ چاہے عقد کتابت پر رہے اور چاہے ام ولد ر ہے۔ اب اگر اس نے پہلی صورت اختیار کی یعنی بدل کتابت ادا کر کے فی الحال آزاد ہونا چاہا تو وہ آقا سے اپنا عقر یعنی میشل وصول کر لے گی۔ امام مالک واحمد اور ایک قول میں امام شافعی بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں ۔ دلیل وہی ہے جو کتابت فاسدہ والی فصل سے کچھ پہلے گزر چکی انها صارت اخص با جز اٹھا کہ مکاتبہ مذکورہ کو اپنی ذات اور اپنے منافع کا اختصاص حاصل ہے۔ قوله ثم ان مسات المولى ... الخ - مکتبہ مذکورہ نے عقد کتابت پر باقی رہنا اختیار کیا اور را در کتابت سے پہلے آقا کا انتقال ہو گیا۔ تو وہ ام ولد ہونے کی وجہ سے آزاد ہو جائے گی اور اس کے ذمہ سے بدل کتابت ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ جس میں کوئی اختلاف نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ مکاتبہ نے مال کا التزام اسی لئے کیا تھا تا کہ اس کا رقبہ اس کو کتابت کی جہت سے سالم ملے۔ حالانکہ یہاں اس جہت سے نہیں ملا۔ لہذا ابدل واجب نہ ہوگا۔
قوله وان ماتت هی.... الخ - اور اگر آقا سے پہلے خود مکاتبہ باندی بن مرگئی اور اس نے کچھ مال چھوڑا ۔ تو اس مال سے اس کا بدل کتابت ادا کیا جائے گا۔ اور اداء بدل کے بعد جو کچھ مال باقی رہے وہ مقتضائے کتابت کے بموجب اس کے بچہ کے لئے میراث ہو گا ( امام احمد کے نزدیک اور ایک قول میں امام شافعی کے نزدیک جو کچھ مکاتبہ کے قبضہ میں وہ آقا کا ہوگا ) اور اگر اس نے کچھ مال نہیں چھوڑا تو بچہ کے ذمہ سعایت نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ وہ آزاد ہے۔
قوله ولو ولدت الخ - اگر مکاتبہ مذکورہ ایک بچہ کے بعد دوسرا بچہ بنے تو آقا کے ذمہ (اس کے سکور کی صورت میں ) لازم نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ام ولد کے بچہ کا نسب سکوت کی صورت میں اس وقت ثابت ہوتا ہے جب آقا کے لئے اس سے وطی کرنا حلال ہو۔ حالانکہ وہ یہاں ایسی ام ولد ہے کہ آقا کے لئے اس سے وطی کرنا حلال نہیں حرام ہے۔ اس لئے آقا کی طرف دعوی نسب کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔ اس کے بغیر وہ دوسرا بچہ اس کے ذمہ لازم نہ ہوگا۔ اب اگر اس نے دوسرے بچہ کے نسب کا دعوی نہ کیا اور مکاتبہ مذکورہ اداء بدل کتابت کے الائق مال چھوڑے بغیر مرگئی تو یہ دوسرا بچہ اداء بدل کتابت کے لئے سعایت کرے گا۔ کیونکہ وہ اپنی ماں کی تبعیت میں مکاتب ہے۔ پھر اگر موت مکاتبہ کے بعد اداء بدل سے پہلے آقا مر گیا۔ تو یہ دو سرا بچہ آزاد ہو جائے گا اور اس کے ذمہ سے سعایت ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ اس لئے کہ یہ بچہ بمنزلہ ام ولد ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ ام ولد کا بچہ ہے تو اس کے تابع ہوگا۔ پس جیسے آقا کی موت کے بعد ام ولد سعایت نہیں کرتی ایسے ہی یہ بچہ بھی نہیں کرے گا۔
آقا نے ام ولد کو مکاتب بنا دیا تو جائز ہے
قال و اذا كاتب المولى ام ولده جاز لحاجتها الى استفادة الحرية قبل موت المولى وذلك بالكتابة ولا تنافى بينهما لأنه تلقتها جهنا حرية فان مات المولى عتقت بالاستيلاد لتعلق عتقها بموت السيد وسقط عنها بدل الكتابة لأن الغرض من اينجاب البدل العتق عند الاداء فاذا عتقت قبله لا يمكن توفير الغرض عليه فسقط وبطلت الكتابة لامتناع ابقائها من غير فائدة غير انه تسلم لها الاكساب والاولاد لان الكتابة انفسخت في حق البدل وبقيت فى حق الاولاد والاكساب لان الفسخ لنظرها والنظر فيما ذكرنا ولو ادت المكاتبة قبل موت المولى عتقت بالكتابة لانها باقية
ترجمہ اگر آقا نے اپنی اتم والد کو مکاتب کر دیا تو جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کو آقا کی موت سے پہلے آزادی حاصل کرنے کی احتیاج ہے اور یہ کتابت ہی سے حاصل ہوگی۔ اور ان دونوں میں کوئی منافات نہیں۔ کیونکہ اس کو حریت کی دو جہتیں حاصل ہیں۔ پھر اگر آقا مر گیا تو ام ولد ہونے کی وجہ سے آزاد ہو جائے گی۔ آقا کی موت کے ساتھ اس کی آزادی متعلق ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ اور اس سے بدل کتابت ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ بدل واجب کرنے سے غرض آزاد ہو جاتا تھا ادا ئیگی کے وقت اور جب وہ اس سے پہلے ہی آزاد ہو گئی تو تو فیر غرض ممکن نہیں رہی لہذا مال ساقط ہو گیا۔ اور کتابت باطل ہو گئی۔ اس کو بے فائدہ باقی رکھنے کے ممتنع ہونے کی وجہ ے ۔ لیکن اتنی بات ہے کہ اس کو
Book of Mukatab. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah volume 12. Acting upon the kitaba, and if she left no wealth, then no sa'y will be upon the child because he is free. And if she gave birth to another child, it will not be necessary upon the master unless he claims it, because intercourse with a mukatabah is forbidden for the master. Now if the master did not claim the child and the mukatabah died without leaving anything, this second child will perform sa'y because he is a mukatab following his mother. Then if after that the master dies, this child will become free and the sa'y will be dropped from his liability because this child is like a child of umm walad, so he follows her. Explanation of 'his saying: and when she gives birth...' - The master made his slave girl a mukatabah and she had a child, then the slave girl has a choice: either to remain upon the kitaba contract and pay the kitaba price and become free immediately, or to declare herself incapable and become umm walad, and after the master's death she will become free. The reason for the choice is that she has obtained the right to freedom from two aspects: one from the aspect of kitaba, and one from becoming umm walad. So she will have the choice of both. 'His saying: and the lineage of her child...' - The lineage of the child of the mentioned mukatabah will be established from the master, whether her birth was at six months or more. And that child will be free, and there is no disagreement on this. The reason is that the master can free her child, because claiming lineage from the master is like emancipation, and if the master can intentionally free a child that is not from his own sperm, then by way of first priority he can do so through claiming lineage. 'His saying: and his property from ownership...' - The word 'property' is from the speech, meaning 'and that which is for him' and 'from ownership' is clarification. The author of Hidayah intends to remove a misunderstanding: one might think that the ownership the master has in the mukatabah is deficient, so claiming lineage should be valid. The author says that the master's ownership of the substance (raqabah) in the mukatabah slave girl is sufficient for the validity of claiming lineage, even if he does not have possession over her. The reason is that this ownership of the master is stronger than the ownership the mukatab has over his mukatabah. Evidence: the master's freeing of his mukatabah is valid, but the mukatab's freeing is not valid. And the ruling is that if a mukatab claims lineage of his mukatabah's child, lineage is established. So when the master is the claimant of lineage, it is established by first priority. 'His saying: and when she passes...' - At the beginning of the issue, it was known that the mentioned mukatabah has two choices: either to remain upon the kitaba contract or become umm walad. Now if she chose the first option, i.e., she wants to become free immediately by paying the kitaba price, then she will receive her 'aqr (compensation) from the master. Imam Malik, Ahmad, and in one opinion Imam Shafi'i also hold this view. The evidence is what was mentioned earlier in the chapter on invalid kitaba: that she has become an exclusive owner of her own self and her profits. 'His saying: then if the master died...' - The mentioned mukatabah chose to remain upon the kitaba contract, and before completing the kitaba the master died. Then she will become free due to being umm walad, and the kitaba price will be dropped from her liability, and there is no disagreement on this. Because the mukatabah undertook the payment only so that her substance would be preserved for her through the kitaba, but here it was not preserved through that avenue, so the price is not obligatory. 'His saying: and if she died...' - And if before the master the mukatabah slave girl herself died and she left some wealth, then from that wealth her kitaba price will be paid, and after payment whatever wealth remains will be inheritance for her child according to the kitaba rule (according to Imam Ahmad and in one opinion Imam Shafi'i, whatever the mukatabah possessed belongs to the master). And if she left no wealth, then no sa'y will be upon the child because he is free. 'His saying: and if she gives birth...' - If the mentioned mukatabah gave birth to a second child after the first, then in case of the master's silence, it will not be necessary upon the master because the lineage of the child of umm walad is established in the case of silence only when intercourse with her is halal for the master. But here it is such an umm walad that intercourse with her is not halal for the master, it is haram. Therefore, the master's claim of lineage is necessary. Without it, that second child will not be necessary upon him. Now if he did not claim lineage of the second child and the mentioned mukatabah died without leaving wealth sufficient for the kitaba price, then this second child will perform sa'y to pay the kitaba price because he is a mukatab following his mother. Then if after the death of the mukatabah and before payment, the master died, this second child will become free and the sa'y will be dropped from his liability because this child is like a child of umm walad, and he follows her. So just as after the master's death the umm walad does not perform sa'y, similarly this child will not. The master made his umm walad a mukatab, it is valid. He said: And if the master makes his umm walad a mukatab, it is valid due to her need to obtain freedom before the master's death, and that is through kitaba. And there is no contradiction between them because she has two aspects of freedom. Then if the master dies, she becomes free due to being umm walad because her freedom is attached to the master's death, and the kitaba price is dropped from her because the purpose of imposing the price was freedom upon payment, and when she becomes free before that, the purpose cannot be achieved, so it is dropped and the kitaba becomes invalid because it is not possible to keep it without benefit. However, she receives the earnings and children because the kitaba is dissolved with respect to the price but remains with respect to children and earnings because the dissolution is for her benefit, and the benefit is as we mentioned. And if the mukatabah pays before the master's death, she becomes free by kitaba because it remains.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from Ashraf al-Hidayah (Urdu sharh of al-Hidayah) covering the rulings of kitaba (contract of manumission) when a mukatabah (female slave under kitaba) becomes pregnant. The commentary follows the order of the matn and expands on each ruling with reasoning. The first key ruling: if a mukatabah gives birth, she has a choice between remaining under the kitaba contract (and paying to become free immediately) or declaring herself incapable and becoming umm walad (mother of the master's child), which grants her freedom upon the master's death. The reason is that she has two avenues to freedom: kitaba and istilad (becoming umm walad). The child's lineage is established from the master, and the child is free, with no disagreement among scholars. The commentary explains that the master's ownership in the mukatabah, though deficient (since she has some rights), is sufficient for claiming lineage because it is stronger than the mukatab's ownership over his own mukatabah. If she chooses to pay and free herself, she is entitled to receive her 'aqr (compensation) from the master, a view held by Imam Malik, Ahmad, and in one narration Imam Shafi'i. If the master dies before she completes payment, she becomes free as umm walad and the kitaba price is dropped; this is agreed upon. If she dies before the master, her wealth is used to pay the kitaba price, and the remainder goes to her child as inheritance (contra Imam Ahmad and some Shafi'i who say it goes to the master). If she leaves no wealth, the child is not liable for sa'y. For a second child born after the first, if the master remains silent, the child's lineage is not established because intercourse with a mukatabah is haram for the master; thus the master must claim it. If he does not claim and she dies without wealth, the second child must perform sa'y to pay the kitaba price. However, if the master dies before payment, the child becomes free and sa'y is dropped because the child is like an umm walad's child. Finally, the master making his umm walad a mukatabah is valid because she needs freedom before his death. If he dies, she becomes free and the kitaba price is dropped. If she pays before his death, she becomes free by kitaba. The commentary uses analogy (qiyas) and istihsan to derive rulings, and references differences with other madhahib where applicable.

Key Terms
مکاتبہ (mukatabah): A female slave who has entered into a kitaba contract (agreement to pay for her freedom in installments).
ام ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who bears a child from her master, becoming free upon his death.
سعایت (sa'y): Effort or earning to pay off the kitaba price; here used for the child's obligation to earn and pay.
نسب (nasab): Lineage or paternity; here established from the master upon his claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the status of a child born to a mukatabah during the kitaba contract?
A) The child is a mukatab and must pay the kitaba price.
B) The child is free and his lineage is from the master.
C) The child becomes an umm walad.
D) The child's status depends on the mother's choice.

Key Takeaway
A mukatabah's child is free and lineage is from the master; the mother has a choice between completing kitaba or becoming umm walad.

Second Child, Aqr, and Master's Death in Mukatabah
Continuation of mukatabah rulings for second child, aqr, and master's death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rulings on the mukatabah's second child (need for master's claim), her entitlement to 'aqr, and the effects of the master's death.

Core Idea
A second child requires master's claim; the mukatabah is entitled to 'aqr; master's death frees her and drops kitaba.

Building on the basic rulings, this lesson addresses more complex scenarios: a second child born during kitaba, the mother's right to compensation ('aqr), and the consequences of the master's death. These rulings illustrate Hanafi reasoning using istihsan and qiyas, and highlight differences with other schools.

Guided Path
1
Examine the second child's ruling
Unlike the first child, the second child's lineage is not automatic; the master must claim it. Reason: intercourse with a mukatabah is haram, so silence does not imply acknowledgment.
This distinction is based on the prohibition of sexual relations with a mukatabah.
2
Understand the sa'y obligation for the second child
If the mother dies without wealth and the master did not claim the second child, that child must perform sa'y (earn to pay the kitaba price) because he follows the mother's contractual status.
This is a form of vicarious liability due to following the mother.
3
Analyze the 'aqr entitlement
If the mukatabah chooses to free herself by paying the kitaba price, she is entitled to receive 'aqr (compensation) from the master. This is based on istihsan, using the analogy of invalid kitaba where she becomes exclusive owner of herself.
Imam Malik, Ahmad, and one opinion of Shafi'i agree; this is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
4
Determine the effect of master's death
If the master dies before she completes the kitaba, she becomes free as umm walad and the kitaba price is dropped. If she dies first, her wealth pays the kitaba, remainder to her child (contra some schools).
The Hanafi view prioritizes the child as heir over the master's residual ownership.
5
Apply the ruling on making umm walad a mukatab
A master may validly make his umm walad a mukatabah; she then has two paths to freedom. If she pays before his death, she becomes free by kitaba; if he dies first, she becomes free as umm walad and kitaba drops.
This shows the principle of overlapping causes.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲ ہوگا۔ مقتضائے کتابت پر چلتے ہوئے اور اگر اس نے کچھ مال نہیں چھوڑا تو بچہ پر سعایت نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ وہ آزاد ہے۔ اور اگر اسنے دوسرا بچہ جنا تو ہر آقا کے ذمہ لازم نہ ہوگا ۔ مگر یہ کہ وہ دعوی کرے کیونکہ آقا پر مکاتبہ کی وطی حرام ہے۔ اب اگر آقا نے بچہ کا دعویٰ نہیں کیا اور مکاتبہ کچھ چھوڑے بغیر مرگئی تو یہ دوسرا بچہ سعایت کرے گا۔ اس لئے کہ وہ ماں کے تابع ہو کر مکاتب ہے۔ پھر اگر اس کے بعد آ قا مر جائے تو یہ بچہ آزاد ہو جائے گا اور اس کے ذمہ سے سعایت ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ یہ بچہ بمنزلہ ولد کے ہے اس لئے کہ وہ ام ولد کا بچہ ہے تو اسی کے تابع ہوگا۔

قوله ونسب ولدها .... الخ - مکاتبہ مذکورہ کے بچہ کا نسب آقا سے ثابت ہوگا۔ خواہ اس کی پیدائش چھ ماہ پر ہوئی ہو یا اس سے زائد پر۔ اور وہ بچہ آزاد ہوگا جس میں کوئی اختلاف نہیں ہے وجہ یہ ہے کہ آقا اس کے بچہ کو آزاد کر سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ آقا کی جانب سے نسب کا دعوی مثل تحریر کے ہے اور جب آقا بالقصد اس کے اس بچہ کو آزاد کر سکتا ہے جو خود اس کے نطفہ سے نہیں ہے تو دعوی نسب کے ضمن میں بطریق اولی کر سکتا ہے۔
قوله وماله من الملک الخ - لفظ مالہ مسیح کلام ہے ای والذی لہ اور من الملک ما کا بیان ہے۔ اس قول سے صاحب ہدایہ کا مقصد ایک وہم کا ازالہ ہے۔ وہم یہ ہوتا ہے کہ مکاتبہ میں جو آقا کی ملک ہے وہ ناقص ہے۔ لہذا اس کی طرف سے دعوی نسب صحیح ہونا چاہیے۔ موصوف فرماتے ہیں کہ آقا کو مکاتبہ باندی میں جو ملک رقبہ حاصل ہے وہ صحت دعوئی استیلا د کے لئے کافی ہے گو اس کو ملک ید حاصل نہ ہو۔ وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ آقا کی یہ ملک بہر حال اس ملک سے قوی تر ہے۔ جو مکاتب کو اپنی مکاتبہ میں حاصل ہوتی ہے۔ بدلیل آنکہ آقا کا اپنی مکاتبہ کو آزاد کر نا صیح ہے اور مکاتب کا آزاد کر ناصحیح نہیں۔ اور مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مکاتب اگر اپنی مکاتبہ کے بچہ کا نسب کا دعوی کرے تو اس سے نسب ثابت ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس جب آقا مدعی نسب ہو تو بطریق اولی ثابت ہوگا۔
قوله واذا مضت ... الخ - آغاز مسئلہ میں یہ بات معلوم ہوگئی تھی کہ مکاتبہ مذکورہ کود و اختیار ہیں ۔ چاہے عقد کتابت پر رہے اور چاہے ام ولد ر ہے۔ اب اگر اس نے پہلی صورت اختیار کی یعنی بدل کتابت ادا کر کے فی الحال آزاد ہونا چاہا تو وہ آقا سے اپنا عقر یعنی میشل وصول کر لے گی۔ امام مالک واحمد اور ایک قول میں امام شافعی بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں ۔ دلیل وہی ہے جو کتابت فاسدہ والی فصل سے کچھ پہلے گزر چکی انها صارت اخص با جز اٹھا کہ مکاتبہ مذکورہ کو اپنی ذات اور اپنے منافع کا اختصاص حاصل ہے۔ قوله ثم ان مسات المولى ... الخ - مکتبہ مذکورہ نے عقد کتابت پر باقی رہنا اختیار کیا اور را در کتابت سے پہلے آقا کا انتقال ہو گیا۔ تو وہ ام ولد ہونے کی وجہ سے آزاد ہو جائے گی اور اس کے ذمہ سے بدل کتابت ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ جس میں کوئی اختلاف نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ مکاتبہ نے مال کا التزام اسی لئے کیا تھا تا کہ اس کا رقبہ اس کو کتابت کی جہت سے سالم ملے۔ حالانکہ یہاں اس جہت سے نہیں ملا۔ لہذا ابدل واجب نہ ہوگا۔
قوله وان ماتت هی.... الخ - اور اگر آقا سے پہلے خود مکاتبہ باندی بن مرگئی اور اس نے کچھ مال چھوڑا ۔ تو اس مال سے اس کا بدل کتابت ادا کیا جائے گا۔ اور اداء بدل کے بعد جو کچھ مال باقی رہے وہ مقتضائے کتابت کے بموجب اس کے بچہ کے لئے میراث ہو گا ( امام احمد کے نزدیک اور ایک قول میں امام شافعی کے نزدیک جو کچھ مکاتبہ کے قبضہ میں وہ آقا کا ہوگا ) اور اگر اس نے کچھ مال نہیں چھوڑا تو بچہ کے ذمہ سعایت نہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ وہ آزاد ہے۔
قوله ولو ولدت الخ - اگر مکاتبہ مذکورہ ایک بچہ کے بعد دوسرا بچہ بنے تو آقا کے ذمہ (اس کے سکور کی صورت میں ) لازم نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ام ولد کے بچہ کا نسب سکوت کی صورت میں اس وقت ثابت ہوتا ہے جب آقا کے لئے اس سے وطی کرنا حلال ہو۔ حالانکہ وہ یہاں ایسی ام ولد ہے کہ آقا کے لئے اس سے وطی کرنا حلال نہیں حرام ہے۔ اس لئے آقا کی طرف دعوی نسب کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔ اس کے بغیر وہ دوسرا بچہ اس کے ذمہ لازم نہ ہوگا۔ اب اگر اس نے دوسرے بچہ کے نسب کا دعوی نہ کیا اور مکاتبہ مذکورہ اداء بدل کتابت کے الائق مال چھوڑے بغیر مرگئی تو یہ دوسرا بچہ اداء بدل کتابت کے لئے سعایت کرے گا۔ کیونکہ وہ اپنی ماں کی تبعیت میں مکاتب ہے۔ پھر اگر موت مکاتبہ کے بعد اداء بدل سے پہلے آقا مر گیا۔ تو یہ دو سرا بچہ آزاد ہو جائے گا اور اس کے ذمہ سے سعایت ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ اس لئے کہ یہ بچہ بمنزلہ ام ولد ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ ام ولد کا بچہ ہے تو اس کے تابع ہوگا۔ پس جیسے آقا کی موت کے بعد ام ولد سعایت نہیں کرتی ایسے ہی یہ بچہ بھی نہیں کرے گا۔
آقا نے ام ولد کو مکاتب بنا دیا تو جائز ہے
قال و اذا كاتب المولى ام ولده جاز لحاجتها الى استفادة الحرية قبل موت المولى وذلك بالكتابة ولا تنافى بينهما لأنه تلقتها جهنا حرية فان مات المولى عتقت بالاستيلاد لتعلق عتقها بموت السيد وسقط عنها بدل الكتابة لأن الغرض من اينجاب البدل العتق عند الاداء فاذا عتقت قبله لا يمكن توفير الغرض عليه فسقط وبطلت الكتابة لامتناع ابقائها من غير فائدة غير انه تسلم لها الاكساب والاولاد لان الكتابة انفسخت في حق البدل وبقيت فى حق الاولاد والاكساب لان الفسخ لنظرها والنظر فيما ذكرنا ولو ادت المكاتبة قبل موت المولى عتقت بالكتابة لانها باقية
ترجمہ اگر آقا نے اپنی اتم والد کو مکاتب کر دیا تو جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کو آقا کی موت سے پہلے آزادی حاصل کرنے کی احتیاج ہے اور یہ کتابت ہی سے حاصل ہوگی۔ اور ان دونوں میں کوئی منافات نہیں۔ کیونکہ اس کو حریت کی دو جہتیں حاصل ہیں۔ پھر اگر آقا مر گیا تو ام ولد ہونے کی وجہ سے آزاد ہو جائے گی۔ آقا کی موت کے ساتھ اس کی آزادی متعلق ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ اور اس سے بدل کتابت ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ بدل واجب کرنے سے غرض آزاد ہو جاتا تھا ادا ئیگی کے وقت اور جب وہ اس سے پہلے ہی آزاد ہو گئی تو تو فیر غرض ممکن نہیں رہی لہذا مال ساقط ہو گیا۔ اور کتابت باطل ہو گئی۔ اس کو بے فائدہ باقی رکھنے کے ممتنع ہونے کی وجہ ے ۔ لیکن اتنی بات ہے کہ اس کو
Book of Mukatab. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah volume 12. Acting upon the kitaba, and if she left no wealth, then no sa'y will be upon the child because he is free. And if she gave birth to another child, it will not be necessary upon the master unless he claims it, because intercourse with a mukatabah is forbidden for the master. Now if the master did not claim the child and the mukatabah died without leaving anything, this second child will perform sa'y because he is a mukatab following his mother. Then if after that the master dies, this child will become free and the sa'y will be dropped from his liability because this child is like a child of umm walad, so he follows her. Explanation of 'his saying: and when she gives birth...' - The master made his slave girl a mukatabah and she had a child, then the slave girl has a choice: either to remain upon the kitaba contract and pay the kitaba price and become free immediately, or to declare herself incapable and become umm walad, and after the master's death she will become free. The reason for the choice is that she has obtained the right to freedom from two aspects: one from the aspect of kitaba, and one from becoming umm walad. So she will have the choice of both. 'His saying: and the lineage of her child...' - The lineage of the child of the mentioned mukatabah will be established from the master, whether her birth was at six months or more. And that child will be free, and there is no disagreement on this. The reason is that the master can free her child, because claiming lineage from the master is like emancipation, and if the master can intentionally free a child that is not from his own sperm, then by way of first priority he can do so through claiming lineage. 'His saying: and his property from ownership...' - The word 'property' is from the speech, meaning 'and that which is for him' and 'from ownership' is clarification. The author of Hidayah intends to remove a misunderstanding: one might think that the ownership the master has in the mukatabah is deficient, so claiming lineage should be valid. The author says that the master's ownership of the substance (raqabah) in the mukatabah slave girl is sufficient for the validity of claiming lineage, even if he does not have possession over her. The reason is that this ownership of the master is stronger than the ownership the mukatab has over his mukatabah. Evidence: the master's freeing of his mukatabah is valid, but the mukatab's freeing is not valid. And the ruling is that if a mukatab claims lineage of his mukatabah's child, lineage is established. So when the master is the claimant of lineage, it is established by first priority. 'His saying: and when she passes...' - At the beginning of the issue, it was known that the mentioned mukatabah has two choices: either to remain upon the kitaba contract or become umm walad. Now if she chose the first option, i.e., she wants to become free immediately by paying the kitaba price, then she will receive her 'aqr (compensation) from the master. Imam Malik, Ahmad, and in one opinion Imam Shafi'i also hold this view. The evidence is what was mentioned earlier in the chapter on invalid kitaba: that she has become an exclusive owner of her own self and her profits. 'His saying: then if the master died...' - The mentioned mukatabah chose to remain upon the kitaba contract, and before completing the kitaba the master died. Then she will become free due to being umm walad, and the kitaba price will be dropped from her liability, and there is no disagreement on this. Because the mukatabah undertook the payment only so that her substance would be preserved for her through the kitaba, but here it was not preserved through that avenue, so the price is not obligatory. 'His saying: and if she died...' - And if before the master the mukatabah slave girl herself died and she left some wealth, then from that wealth her kitaba price will be paid, and after payment whatever wealth remains will be inheritance for her child according to the kitaba rule (according to Imam Ahmad and in one opinion Imam Shafi'i, whatever the mukatabah possessed belongs to the master). And if she left no wealth, then no sa'y will be upon the child because he is free. 'His saying: and if she gives birth...' - If the mentioned mukatabah gave birth to a second child after the first, then in case of the master's silence, it will not be necessary upon the master because the lineage of the child of umm walad is established in the case of silence only when intercourse with her is halal for the master. But here it is such an umm walad that intercourse with her is not halal for the master, it is haram. Therefore, the master's claim of lineage is necessary. Without it, that second child will not be necessary upon him. Now if he did not claim lineage of the second child and the mentioned mukatabah died without leaving wealth sufficient for the kitaba price, then this second child will perform sa'y to pay the kitaba price because he is a mukatab following his mother. Then if after the death of the mukatabah and before payment, the master died, this second child will become free and the sa'y will be dropped from his liability because this child is like a child of umm walad, and he follows her. So just as after the master's death the umm walad does not perform sa'y, similarly this child will not. The master made his umm walad a mukatab, it is valid. He said: And if the master makes his umm walad a mukatab, it is valid due to her need to obtain freedom before the master's death, and that is through kitaba. And there is no contradiction between them because she has two aspects of freedom. Then if the master dies, she becomes free due to being umm walad because her freedom is attached to the master's death, and the kitaba price is dropped from her because the purpose of imposing the price was freedom upon payment, and when she becomes free before that, the purpose cannot be achieved, so it is dropped and the kitaba becomes invalid because it is not possible to keep it without benefit. However, she receives the earnings and children because the kitaba is dissolved with respect to the price but remains with respect to children and earnings because the dissolution is for her benefit, and the benefit is as we mentioned. And if the mukatabah pays before the master's death, she becomes free by kitaba because it remains.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from Ashraf al-Hidayah (Urdu sharh of al-Hidayah) covering the rulings of kitaba (contract of manumission) when a mukatabah (female slave under kitaba) becomes pregnant. The commentary follows the order of the matn and expands on each ruling with reasoning. The first key ruling: if a mukatabah gives birth, she has a choice between remaining under the kitaba contract (and paying to become free immediately) or declaring herself incapable and becoming umm walad (mother of the master's child), which grants her freedom upon the master's death. The reason is that she has two avenues to freedom: kitaba and istilad (becoming umm walad). The child's lineage is established from the master, and the child is free, with no disagreement among scholars. The commentary explains that the master's ownership in the mukatabah, though deficient (since she has some rights), is sufficient for claiming lineage because it is stronger than the mukatab's ownership over his own mukatabah. If she chooses to pay and free herself, she is entitled to receive her 'aqr (compensation) from the master, a view held by Imam Malik, Ahmad, and in one narration Imam Shafi'i. If the master dies before she completes payment, she becomes free as umm walad and the kitaba price is dropped; this is agreed upon. If she dies before the master, her wealth is used to pay the kitaba price, and the remainder goes to her child as inheritance (contra Imam Ahmad and some Shafi'i who say it goes to the master). If she leaves no wealth, the child is not liable for sa'y. For a second child born after the first, if the master remains silent, the child's lineage is not established because intercourse with a mukatabah is haram for the master; thus the master must claim it. If he does not claim and she dies without wealth, the second child must perform sa'y to pay the kitaba price. However, if the master dies before payment, the child becomes free and sa'y is dropped because the child is like an umm walad's child. Finally, the master making his umm walad a mukatabah is valid because she needs freedom before his death. If he dies, she becomes free and the kitaba price is dropped. If she pays before his death, she becomes free by kitaba. The commentary uses analogy (qiyas) and istihsan to derive rulings, and references differences with other madhahib where applicable.

Key Terms
مکاتبہ (mukatabah): A female slave who has entered into a kitaba contract.
ام ولد (umm walad): A slave woman who bears a child from her master, becoming free upon his death.
سعایت (sa'y): Effort to pay kitaba price; here child's obligation.
عقر ('aqr): Compensation paid to mukatabah when she frees herself, equivalent to deficiency in value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to a second child born to a mukatabah if the master remains silent?
A) The child is free and lineage established from the master.
B) The child becomes an umm walad.
C) The child is not attached to the master and must perform sa'y if the mother dies without wealth.
D) The master automatically owns the child.

Key Takeaway
The second child requires the master's claim; the mother is entitled to 'aqr; the master's death frees the umm walad and drops the kitaba.

Settling Deferred Kitabah for Immediate Payment: Istihsan vs Qiyas
Ruling on settling deferred kitabah for immediate payment via istihsan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits a mukatab to settle a deferred kitabah payment for a lesser immediate amount, and evaluate the qiyas objection.

Core Idea
Reducing deferred kitabah for immediate payment is permissible by istihsan, not qiyas, due to the unique nature of kitabah.

This passage examines a specific transaction: a master reduces the kitabah payment from 1,000 dirhams due in one year to 500 dirhams immediate. By qiyas, this appears to be riba, but the Hanafi school permits it via istihsan. The lesson unpacks the legal reasoning, the distinction from free persons, and the intra- and inter-madhhab disputes.

Guided Path
1
State the transaction and the Hanafi ruling
Identify the case: a master and his mukatab slave agree to reduce the deferred kitabah amount for immediate payment. The Hanafi ruling is that it is permissible (mubah) by istihsan.
The ruling is contrary to what qiyas would dictate.
2
Understand the qiyas analogy
By qiyas, the settlement is likened to a free person reducing a debt for early payment, which is riba. The illa (effective cause) is compensation for time, which is not property.
This is the position of Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and within Hanafi, Abu Yusuf and Zufar.
3
Analyze the istihsan justification
Istihsan argues that time is considered property for the mukatab because he cannot pay without the extension. The kitabah payment itself is only partially property (surety is invalid), so they balance out, preventing riba.
This creates a shubhat al-shabah (semblance of a semblance) of riba, which is not legally significant.
4
Distinguish from the free person case
In a contract between free persons, both parties exchange full property, and time has no property value, making reduction for early payment unequivocally riba.
The uniqueness of the kitabah contract lies in its partial commutative nature and the slave's dependency on time.
5
Identify the dispute and thamarah al-khilaf
The Hanafi position (istihsan) is opposed by other schools and some Hanafi scholars. The practical consequence: Hanafis allow the settlement; others prohibit it as riba.
The relied-upon position is istihsan, based on the authority of the majority of Hanafi masters.

نال وان كاتبه على الف درهم الى سنة فصالحه على خمس مائة معجلة فهو جائز استحسانا وفي القياس لا جوز لانه اعتياض عن الاجل وهو ليس بمال والدين مال فكان ربوا وهذا لا يجوز مثله في الحر ومكاتب الغير وجه الاستحسان ان الاجل فى حق المكاتب مال من وجه لانه لا يقدر على الاداء الا به فاعطى له حكم المال وبدل الكتابة مال من وجه حتى لا تصح الكفالة به فاعتدلا فلا يكون ربوا ولان عقد الكتابة عقد من وجه دون وجه و الاجل ربوا من وجه فيكون شبهة الشبهة بخلاف العقد بين الحرين لانه عقد كل وجه فكان ربوا والاجل فيه شبهة
ترجمہ اگر ملوک کو ایک سال کے وعدے سے ایک ہزار درہم پر مکاتب کیا۔ پھر فوری پانچ سو پر صلح کرلی تو یہ جائز ہے استحسانا اور قیاس میں جائز نہیں کیونکہ یہ میعاد کا عوض لینا ہے اور میعاد مال نہیں ہے اور دین مذکور مال ہے تو یہ مباح ہوا اسی لئے آزاد اور مکاتب غیر کی صورت میں ایسا جائز نہیں ہوتا۔ وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ مکاتب کے حق میں میعاد بھی ایک طرح کا مال ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ میعاد کے بغیر ادا ئیگی پر قادر نہیں تو میعاد کو مال کا حکم دے دیا گیا۔ اور بدل کتابت بھی ایک طرح سے مال ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ اس کی کفالت صحیح نہیں ہوتی ۔ پس دونوں برابر ہو گئے ۔ لہذا بیاج نہ ہوگا۔ اور اس لئے کہ عقد کتابت ایک وجہ سے عقد ہے دوسری وجہ سے نہیں ہے اور میعاد بھی ایک وجہ سے بیاج ہے تو یہاں شہبتہ اشبہ ہوا۔ بخلاف اس عقد کے جو دو آزاد شخصوں میں ہو کہ وہ ہر طرح سے عقد ہے تو بیاج ہو گیا۔ اور میعاد میں بیاج کا شبہ ہے۔ تشریح... قوله وان كاتبه على الف ... الخ اگر آقا نے اپنے مملوک کو یک سالہ میعادی ہزار درہم پر مکاتب کیا پھر اس کے عوض میں پانچ سونقد پر صلح کرلی تو یہ استحسانا جائز ہے۔ از روئے قیاس جائز نہیں۔ چنانچہ امام مالک اور امام شافعی اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ اور حلیہ میں ہے کہ امام ابو یوسف اور امام زفر کا قول بھی یہی ہے۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں میعاد کا عوض لینا لازم آتا ہے حالانکہ میعاد مال نہیں ہے تو یہ سود ہو گیا ۔ اس کی توضیح یہ ہے کہ جب مملوک نے پانچ سو درہم ادا کئے تو یہ پانچ سو درہم ان ہزار درہموں میں سے پانچ سو کے مقابلہ میں ہوئے جو اس کے ذمہ دین ہیں اور باقی پانچ سو مکاتب کے لئے مدت کے عوض میں سالم رہے حالانکہ مدت مال نہیں ہے اور جو دین اس کے ذمہ ہے وہ مال ہے پس یہ مقابلہ مال بلا مال ہوا اور یہی سود ہے(لان الـربـوا هـو الفضل الحالي عن العوض ) یہی وجہ ہے کہ آزاد کی صورت میں اور غیر کے مکاتب کی صورت میں ایسا معاملہ جائز نہیں ہوتا۔ مثلاً ایک آزاد شخص پر یا زید کے مکاتب پر ہزار درہم ادھار ہوں جن کی میعاد ایک سال ہے اور وہ نقد پانچ سو درہم پر صلح کریں تو یہ جائز نہیں ہے۔
قوله وجه الاستحسان.... الخ - وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ مدت گوفی نفسہ مال نہیں لیکن غلام کے حق میں وہ مال ہی کے حکم میں ہے۔ بایں معنی کہ وہ مدت کے بغیر بدل کتابت ادا کرنے پر قادر نہیں۔ اور بدل کتابت بھی صرف من وجہ مال ہے۔ من کل الوجوہ مال نہیں ہے ورنہ اس کی کفالت صیحیح ہوتی حالانکہ بدل کتابت کی کفالت صحیح نہیں ۔ پس اس لحاظ سے دونوں برابر ہوئے اور سود لازم نہ آیا۔ قوله ولان عقد الكتابة.... الخ - استحسانی حکم کی دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ عقد کتابت بیچ کے پیش نظر عقد معاوضہ ہے اور غلام کے لحاظ سے معاوضہ نہیں ہے اور حقیقی بیاج دو مالوں کے درمیان ہوتا ہے۔ حالانکہ میعاد ایک وجہ سے مال نہیں ہے تو یہاں بیاج کا شبہ نہیں ہوا ۔ بلکہ شہرة الشبہ ہوا جو معتبر نہیں ہے۔ بخلاف اس کے جب یہ معاملہ دو آزاد شخصوں کے درمیان ہو کہ وہ ہر طرح سے عقد مالی ہے اور میعاد میں بیاج کا شبہ ہے تو یہ معتبر ہو کر بیاج ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ بیاج کا شبہ بمنزلہ بیاج کے ہوتا ہے۔
Section: And if he made a kitabah contract for a thousand dirhams payable in one year, then he settled for five hundred immediate, it is permissible by istihsan, and by qiyas it is not permissible, because it is compensation for time which is not property, and the debt is property, so it would be riba. And this is not permissible in the case of a free person or a mukatab belonging to another. The reason for istihsan is that time, in the right of the mukatab, is property in some aspect, because he cannot pay without it, so it is given the ruling of property. And the kitabah payment is property in some aspect, to the extent that suretyship for it is not valid, so they balance and riba does not occur. And because the kitabah contract is a contract in some aspects and not in others, and time is riba in some aspects, so there is a semblance of a semblance (shubhat al-shabah). Contrary to a contract between two free persons, which is a contract in all respects, so it would be riba, and time therein is a semblance. Translation: If the master made his slave a mukatab for a thousand dirhams due in one year, then settled for five hundred immediate, this is permissible by istihsan, not by qiyas, because it is taking compensation for time, and time is not property, while the debt is property, so it becomes riba. That is why such a transaction is not permissible in the case of a free person or the mukatab of another. The reason for istihsan: time, in the right of the mukatab, is a kind of property, because he cannot pay without it, so time is given the ruling of property. And the kitabah payment is also a kind of property, to the extent that suretyship for it is not valid. Thus they become equal, so no riba. And because the kitabah contract is a contract in one aspect and not in another, and time is riba in one aspect, so there is a semblance of a semblance. Unlike a contract between two free persons, which is a contract in every aspect, so it becomes riba, and time in it is a semblance. Commentary on the statement: 'And if he made a kitabah contract...' - If the master made his slave a mukatab for a thousand dirhams payable in one year, then settled for five hundred cash, this is permissible by istihsan. By qiyas it is not permissible. Thus Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i hold this view. And in al-Hilya it is mentioned that Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Zufar also say this. Because in this case, taking compensation for time is necessary, while time is not property, so it becomes riba. The explanation is: when the slave pays five hundred dirhams, these five hundred correspond to five hundred of the thousand that are a debt on him, and the remaining five hundred remain as compensation for time, while time is not property, and the debt on him is property. Thus this is a exchange of property for non-property, which is riba. That is why in the case of a free person or the mukatab of another, such a transaction is not permissible. For example, if a free person owes a thousand dirhams due in one year, and he settles for five hundred cash, it is not permissible. Statement: 'The reason for istihsan...' - The reason for istihsan is that time in itself is not property, but in the slave's right it is in the ruling of property, because he cannot pay the kitabah payment without time. And the kitabah payment is property only in one aspect, not in all aspects, otherwise suretyship for it would be valid, whereas suretyship for kitabah payment is not valid. So from this perspective they are equal, and riba does not become necessary. Statement: 'And because the kitabah contract...' - The second proof for the istihsani ruling is that the kitabah contract, from the perspective of the exchange, is a commutative contract, but from the slave's perspective it is not commutative. And real riba occurs between two properties. Since time is not property in one aspect, there is no semblance of riba here; rather it is a semblance of a semblance, which is not significant. Unlike when this transaction is between two free persons: that is a financial contract in every aspect, and time has a semblance of riba, so it becomes riba, because a semblance of riba is like riba itself.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage deals with a specific scenario: a master makes his slave a mukatab for 1,000 dirhams payable in one year, then later agrees to reduce the amount to 500 dirhams in exchange for immediate payment. The question is whether this is permissible. The Hanafi ruling is that it is permissible by istihsan (juristic preference) but not by qiyas (analogy). By qiyas, this would be riba because the master is receiving 500 dirhams now instead of 1,000 later, and the difference compensates for the time value, which is not property. However, istihsan permits it because time has a monetary value for the mukatab: without the extension, he cannot afford to pay. The kitabah payment itself is only partially considered property (since suretyship for it is invalid). Hence, time and the kitabah payment balance out, eliminating riba. Furthermore, the kitabah contract is peculiar: it is a commutative contract from the master's side but not entirely from the slave's side. Thus, the semblance of riba is weak. In contrast, a similar transaction between two free individuals is outright riba because both sides are pure financial obligations. The passage also notes that Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i reject this istihsan and consider it invalid qiyas. Additionally, within the Hanafi school, Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Zufar also hold the qiyas view (disallowing it). The relied-upon Hanafi position is istihsan, allowing it.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; departing from a clear analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more equitable ruling based on a stronger evidence or custom.
ربوا (riba): Usury or interest; any excess in exchange of two fungible goods when the excess is without consideration.
شبهة الشبہ (shubhat al-shabah): A semblance of a semblance; a very weak similarity that does not carry legal weight.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, why is it permissible for a mukatab to settle a 1,000 dirham debt for 500 dirhams immediate payment?
A) Because qiyas allows it
B) Because time is considered property for the mukatab, preventing riba
C) Because both parties are free to agree on any amount
D) Because the master has the right to forgive the debt

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits reducing deferred kitabah for immediate payment via istihsan because time is considered property for the mukatab, preventing riba.

Settlement of Deferred Kitabah Payment by Mukatab
Istihsan ruling on immediate payment in lieu of deferred kitabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on settling a deferred kitabah payment with immediate payment and explain the istihsan argument that treats deferment as property for the mukatab.

Core Idea
Hanafi istihsan treats deferment as property for the mukatab, making settlement valid despite qiyas.

When a mukatab (slave under contract of manumission) owes payments over time, can he settle early with a lump sum at a discount? By strict analogy (qiyas), this resembles riba. But Hanafi jurists, using istihsan, consider the unique nature of kitabah and treat the deferment as property in effect for the mukatab, permitting the settlement. This lesson unpacks that reasoning and the intra-school and inter-school differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and qiyas ruling
The case: master makes slave a mukatab for 1000 dirhams payable in one year, then settles for 500 cash. By qiyas, this is invalid because deferment is not property, so the discount constitutes riba.
2
Understand the istihsan argument
Istihsan holds that for the mukatab, deferment is treated as property because without it he cannot pay. Thus it is given the ruling of property.
This is a departure from qiyas due to hardship.
3
Analyze the balance between deferment and payment
The kitabah payment is also property only in one sense (suretyship for it is invalid). So both sides are equal, and no riba occurs.
Equal in being property 'min wajh'.
4
Contrast with contracts between free men
Between free men, both debt and payment are full property, so a discount for early payment is riba. The kitabah contract is unique: it is a contract in one sense and manumission in another.
5
Note the ikhtilaf and mufta bihi
Imam Malik, Imam Shafi'i, and reportedly Abu Yusuf and Zufar hold the qiyas view. The relied-upon Hanafi position is Abu Hanifa's istihsan, as recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah prefers this view.

قوله وجه الاستحسان.... الخ - وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ مدت گوفی نفسہ مال نہیں لیکن غلام کے حق میں وہ مال ہی کے حکم میں ہے۔ بایں معنی کہ وہ مدت کے بغیر بدل کتابت ادا کرنے پر قادر نہیں۔ اور بدل کتابت بھی صرف من وجہ مال ہے۔ من کل الوجوہ مال نہیں ہے ورنہ اس کی کفالت صیحیح ہوتی حالانکہ بدل کتابت کی کفالت صحیح نہیں ۔ پس اس لحاظ سے دونوں برابر ہوئے اور سود لازم نہ آیا۔ قوله ولان عقد الكتابة.... الخ - استحسانی حکم کی دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ عقد کتابت بیچ کے پیش نظر عقد معاوضہ ہے اور غلام کے لحاظ سے معاوضہ نہیں ہے اور حقیقی بیاج دو مالوں کے درمیان ہوتا ہے۔ حالانکہ میعاد ایک وجہ سے مال نہیں ہے تو یہاں بیاج کا شبہ نہیں ہوا ۔ بلکہ شہرة الشبہ ہوا جو معتبر نہیں ہے۔ بخلاف اس کے جب یہ معاملہ دو آزاد شخصوں کے درمیان ہو کہ وہ ہر طرح سے عقد مالی ہے اور میعاد میں بیاج کا شبہ ہے تو یہ معتبر ہو کر بیاج ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ بیاج کا شبہ بمنزلہ بیاج کے ہوتا ہے۔
That the term (deferment) in the right of the mukatab is property in one sense, because he cannot perform payment except through it, so it is given the ruling of property. And the kitabah payment is property in one sense, such that suretyship for it is not valid. So they become balanced, thus there is no riba. And because the contract of kitabah is a contract in one sense and not in another, and deferment is riba in one sense, so it is a doubt of a doubt. Unlike the contract between two free men, because it is a contract in every sense, so it is riba, and deferment therein is a doubt. Translation: If the master made his slave a mukatab for one thousand dirhams with a one-year deferment, then settled for five hundred immediately, it is valid by istihsan, but not by qiyas, because it is taking compensation for the deferment, and deferment is not property, while the debt mentioned is property, so it becomes permissible. Hence, in the case of a free man or a mukatab of another, it is not valid. The reason for istihsan is that deferment for the mukatab is a kind of property, because he cannot pay without it, so deferment is given the ruling of property. And the kitabah payment is also a kind of property, such that suretyship for it is not valid. So both become equal, thus no riba. Also, because the contract of kitabah is a contract in one sense and not in another, and deferment is riba in one sense, so here it is shubhat al-shubhah. Unlike the contract between two free men, because it is a contract in every sense, so riba occurs, and deferment therein is a doubt. Commentary... The author's statement: 'And if he made him a mukatab for one thousand' etc. If the master made his slave a mukatab for one thousand with a one-year deferment, then settled for five hundred cash, it is valid by istihsan. By qiyas it is not valid. Similarly, Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i hold this view. And in al-Hilyah, it is narrated that Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Zufar also hold this view. Because in this case, taking compensation for the deferment becomes necessary, while deferment is not property, so it becomes usury. Its explanation: When the slave pays five hundred dirhams, these five hundred correspond to five hundred of the thousand that are a debt on him, and the remaining five hundred remain for the mukatab as compensation for the term, while the term is not property and the debt on him is property. So this is an exchange of property for non-property, and that is usury (for usury is a surplus free from compensation). This is why in the case of a free man or the mukatab of another, such a transaction is not valid. For example, if a free man or Zayd's mukatab owes one thousand dirhams on credit with a one-year term, and they settle for five hundred cash, it is not valid. The author's statement: 'The reason for istihsan...' The reason for istihsan is that the term, although not property in itself, is in the ruling of property in the right of the slave, meaning that without the term he is unable to pay the kitabah payment. And the kitabah payment is property only in one sense, not in every sense, otherwise suretyship for it would be valid, whereas suretyship for the kitabah payment is not valid. So from this perspective, both are equal, and usury is not necessitated. The author's statement: 'And because the contract of kitabah...' The second evidence for the istihsani ruling is that the contract of kitabah, from the perspective of exchange, is a commutative contract, but from the perspective of the slave, it is not commutative. And real usury occurs between two properties. Since the term is not property in one sense, here the doubt of usury does not arise; rather, it is a doubt of a doubt, which is not considered. Unlike when this transaction is between two free men, where it is a financial contract in every sense, and the deferment has a doubt of usury, so it is considered and becomes usury. Because a doubt of usury is like usury itself.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof discussing the validity of a settlement (sulh) in a kitabah contract. The case: a master manumits his slave for one thousand dirhams payable in one year. Later, they agree to settle for five hundred dirhams paid immediately. By qiyas, this is invalid because it involves exchanging the debt (property) for an immediate payment, leaving the remaining five hundred as compensation for the deferment, which is not property – constituting riba. However, by istihsan (juristic preference), it is valid. The Hanafi reasoning is that for a mukatab, the deferment is considered property in effect since he cannot pay without it. Similarly, the kitabah payment is not pure property (hence suretyship is invalid). Thus, both sides (deferment and payment) are of similar status, and no riba occurs. The passage contrasts this with contracts between free men, where both elements are pure property, so the duda of riba becomes actual riba. The text also notes that Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i reject this istihsan, and there is a reported view from Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Zufar agreeing with qiyas. The relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi) is the istihsan view, as stated in the commentary.

Key Terms
اجل (ajal): The deferred period in a kitabah contract; in this context, it is considered property in effect for the mukatab.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference departing from qiyas for a stronger reason; here due to the unique nature of kitabah.
کتابت (kitabah): A contract between master and slave for manumission in exchange for payments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is the basis for the Hanafi istihsan allowing settlement of deferred kitabah payment at a discount?
A) The master's consent overrides riba.
B) The slave's inability to pay without deferment makes deferment property.
C) The contract of kitabah is not a real contract.
D) The payment is not yet due.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi fiqh permits a mukatab to settle his deferred kitabah payment at a discount because the deferment is deemed property in effect, balancing the exchange and avoiding riba.
